<p>The <b>2013 Africa Cup of Nations</b>, also known as the <b><a href="/wiki/Orange_S.A." title="Orange S.A.">Orange</a> Africa Cup of Nations South Africa 2013</b> for sponsorship reasons, held from 19 January to 10 February 2013, was the 29th <a href="/wiki/Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="Africa Cup of Nations">Africa Cup of Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> championship of Africa organized by the <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_African_Football" title="Confederation of African Football">Confederation of African Football</a> (CAF).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CAFdecree_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-CAFdecree-1">[1]</a></sup> Starting from this edition, the tournament was switched to being held in odd-numbered years instead of even-numbered years so that it does not clash with the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news.bbc.co.uk_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-news.bbc.co.uk-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>South Africa hosted the tournament for the second time, after previously hosting the <a href="/wiki/1996_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="1996 African Cup of Nations">1996 African Cup of Nations</a>. The 2013 tournament is the highest attended edition of the Africa Cup of Nations under the current, 16-team format. The <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_national_football_team" title="South Africa national football team">South African team</a> was eliminated in the quarter-finals by Mali, following a penalty shoot-out.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Nigeria_national_football_team" title="Nigeria national football team">Nigeria</a> won its third Africa Cup of Nations championship with a 1–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso_national_football_team" title="Burkina Faso national football team">Burkina Faso</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations_Final" title="2013 Africa Cup of Nations Final">final</a>. Nigeria participated in the <a href="/wiki/2013_FIFA_Confederations_Cup" title="2013 FIFA Confederations Cup">2013 FIFA Confederations Cup</a> in Brazil as the representative from CAF.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Host_selection">Host selection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Host selection">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Five countries were put on the shortlist to host the tournament including one joint bid.</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="450" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Flag_of_Angola.svg/23px-Flag_of_Angola.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Flag_of_Angola.svg/35px-Flag_of_Angola.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Flag_of_Angola.svg/45px-Flag_of_Angola.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a></li>

<p>Other countries that failed in their bids were:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="450" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Flag_of_Benin.svg/23px-Flag_of_Benin.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Flag_of_Benin.svg/35px-Flag_of_Benin.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Flag_of_Benin.svg/45px-Flag_of_Benin.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Benin" title="Benin">Benin</a> / <span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="450" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Flag_of_the_Central_African_Republic.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Central_African_Republic.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Flag_of_the_Central_African_Republic.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Central_African_Republic.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Flag_of_the_Central_African_Republic.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Central_African_Republic.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_Botswana.svg/23px-Flag_of_Botswana.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_Botswana.svg/35px-Flag_of_Botswana.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_Botswana.svg/45px-Flag_of_Botswana.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a></li>
</ul>
<p>Originally Libya won the right to host the tournament after defeating a <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigerian</a> bid along with three other bid winning nations, <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a>. Bids from <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a>, <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> were rejected and did not reach the shortlist. For the first time in CAF history, the hosts of three successive tournaments were chosen at the same time; Angola was chosen to host in 2010, Gabon/Equatorial Guinea were chosen as hosts for the 2012 Cup and Libya for the 2013 edition. However, due to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2011_Libyan_Civil_War" title="2011 Libyan Civil War">Libyan Civil War</a>, Libya traded years with South Africa, so that South Africa hosted in 2013 and Libya will be hosting in 2017. This was ratified in September 2011 at CAF's Executive Committee in Cairo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Qualification">Qualification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Qualification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations_qualification" title="2013 Africa Cup of Nations qualification">2013 Africa Cup of Nations qualification</a></div>
<p>A total of 47 countries entered the qualification, including <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_national_football_team" title="South Africa national football team">South Africa</a>, which automatically qualified. <a href="/wiki/Libya_national_football_team" title="Libya national football team">Libya</a> was not allowed to keep its automatic qualification after being stripped of its hosting rights due to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2011_Libyan_Civil_War" title="2011 Libyan Civil War">Libyan Civil War</a>. Many teams made their return to the finals in this tournament. The hosts, South Africa returned after a 4-year absence. Ethiopia appeared for the first time since 1982 (a 31-year absence). Other teams absent from the 2012 finals that featured in 2013 were <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_national_football_team" title="Nigeria national football team">Nigeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Togo_national_football_team" title="Togo national football team">Togo</a>, <a href="/wiki/DR_Congo_national_football_team" title="DR Congo national football team">DR Congo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Algeria_national_football_team" title="Algeria national football team">Algeria</a>. <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde_national_football_team" title="Cape Verde national football team">Cape Verde</a> made its finals debut. Teams that didn't qualify for this tournament from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2012_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="2012 African Cup of Nations">2012 African Cup of Nations</a> were both co-hosts, Gabon and Equatorial Guinea, Libya, Senegal, Sudan, Guinea and Botswana. South Sudan was ineligible to participate as the qualifying competition had already started by the time its membership of CAF was confirmed.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Venues">Venues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Venues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Host_cities">Host cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Host cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/South_African_Football_Association" title="South African Football Association">South African Football Association</a> opened bidding to all <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 FIFA World Cup</a> host cities<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> however a maximum of seven venues would be used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The final list of stadiums was initially to be announced by 30 March,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> but was pushed back to 4 April,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> 20 April, and then 3 May 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>The venues were announced on 4 May 2012. <a href="/wiki/FNB_Stadium" title="FNB Stadium">FNB Stadium</a> hosted the opening match and the final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> The other venues selected for matches were <a href="/wiki/Mbombela_Stadium" title="Mbombela Stadium">Mbombela Stadium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela_Bay_Stadium" title="Nelson Mandela Bay Stadium">Nelson Mandela Bay Stadium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bafokeng_Stadium" title="Royal Bafokeng Stadium">Royal Bafokeng Stadium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moses_Mabhida_Stadium" title="Moses Mabhida Stadium">Moses Mabhida Stadium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>The average daytime temperature of the host cities ranges from 25.0 °C (77.0 °F) to 30.3 °C (86.5 °F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Match_ball">Match ball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Match ball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The official match <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Association_football_(ball)" title="Association football (ball)">ball</a> for the 2013 Africa Cup of Nations was manufactured by <a href="/wiki/Adidas" title="Adidas">Adidas</a> and named the <i>Katlego</i>, which means "success" in <a href="/wiki/Sotho_language" title="Sotho language">Sotho language</a>. The name was chosen by African football fans via an online voting competition where it beat alternate names, <i>Khanya</i> (light) and <i>Motswako</i> (mixture).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascot">Mascot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Mascot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The official mascot of the tournament was Takuma, a <a href="/wiki/Hippopotamus" title="Hippopotamus">hippo</a> wearing sports kit in South Africa's official yellow and green. The mascot was designed by Tumelo Nkoana, a 13-year-old South African student from <a href="/wiki/Hammanskraal" title="Hammanskraal">Hammanskraal</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gauteng" title="Gauteng">Gauteng</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Draw">Draw</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Draw">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The draw for the final tournament took place on 24 October 2012 in <a href="/wiki/Durban" title="Durban">Durban</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Positions A1 and C1 were already assigned to the hosts (South Africa) and holders (Zambia) respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-regulations_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-regulations-20">[20]</a></sup> The other 14 qualified teams were ranked based on their performances during the last three Africa Cup of Nations, i.e. the 2008, 2010 and 2012 editions.</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr>
<th>Classification</th>
<th>Points awarded</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>Winner</th>
<td>7</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>Runner-up</th>
<td>5</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>Losing semi-finalists</th>
<td>3</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>Losing quarter-finalists</th>
<td>2</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>Eliminated in 1st round</th>
<td>1</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Moreover, a weighted coefficient on points was given to each of the last three editions of the Africa Cup of Nations as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/2012_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2012 Africa Cup of Nations">2012 edition</a>: points to be multiplied by 3</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/2010_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2010 Africa Cup of Nations">2010 edition</a>: points to be multiplied by 2</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/2008_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2008 Africa Cup of Nations">2008 edition</a>: points to be multiplied by 1</li>
</ul>
<p>The teams were then divided into four pots based on the ranking. Each group contained one team from each pot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Squads">Squads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Squads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations_squads" title="2013 Africa Cup of Nations squads">2013 Africa Cup of Nations squads</a></div>
<p>Each team can register a squad of 23 players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-regulations_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-regulations-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_stage">Group stage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Group stage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The schedule of the final tournament was released on 8 September 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Tie-breaking criteria</dt>
</dl>
<p>If two or more teams end the group stage with the same number of points, their ranking is determined by the following criteria:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-regulations_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-regulations-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<ol>
<li>points earned in the matches between the teams concerned;</li>
<li>goal difference in the matches between the teams concerned;</li>
<li>number of goals scored in the matches between the teams concerned;</li>
<li>goal difference in all group matches;</li>
<li>number of goals scored in all group matches;</li>
<li>fair play points system taking into account the number of yellow and red cards;</li>
<li>drawing of lots by the organising committee.</li>
</ol>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Knockout_phase">Knockout phase</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Knockout phase">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations_knockout_stage" title="2013 Africa Cup of Nations knockout stage">2013 Africa Cup of Nations knockout stage</a></div>
<p>In the knockout stages, if a match is level at the end of normal playing time, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra_time_(association_football)" title="Extra time (association football)">extra time</a> shall be played (two periods of 15 minutes each) and followed, if necessary, by <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">kicks from the penalty mark</a> to determine the winner, except for the play-off for third place where no extra time shall be played.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-regulations_20-3"><a href="#cite_note-regulations-20">[20]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Quarter-finals">Quarter-finals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Quarter-finals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Goalscorers">Goalscorers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Goalscorers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>4 goals</dt>
</dl>
<div>
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;">
<tr>

<sup><b>(3)</b></sup> – As per statistical convention in football, matches decided in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra_time_(association_football)" title="Extra time (association football)">extra time</a> are counted as wins and losses, while matches decided by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Penalty_shootout_(association_football)" title="Penalty shootout (association football)">penalty shoot-outs</a> are counted as draws.</small>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Marketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorship">Sponsorship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Sponsorship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>South African public broadcaster <a href="/wiki/South_African_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="South African Broadcasting Corporation">SABC</a> was the host broadcaster of the tournament. It paid R65 million (US$7.5 million) for the rights, which entitle it to transmit all of the games across its radio and television platforms.</p>
